#### What this PR does / why we need it:
This PR introduces an alternative mode of pod (or pod slices) placement in TAS: balanced placement. In this placement, Kueue TAS still tries to use the minimum possible number of topology domains but also maximizes the minimum number of pods (or pod slices) placed on a domain. This balancing happens when feature gate `TASBalancedPlacement` is enabled on a level indicated by the user with the `Preferred` flag.

#### Which issue(s) this PR fixes:
<!--
*Automatically closes linked issue when PR is merged.
Usage: `Fixes #<issue number>`, or `Fixes (paste link of issue)`.
_If PR is about `failing-tests or flakes`, please post the related issues/tests in a comment and do not use `Fixes`_*
-->
Fixes #6554 

#### Special notes for your reviewer:

#### Does this PR introduce a user-facing change?
<!--
If no, just write "NONE" in the release-note block below.
If yes, a release note is required:
Enter your extended release note in the block below. If the PR requires additional action from users switching to the new release, include the string "action required".
-->
```release-note
TAS: The balanced placement is introduced with the TASBalancedPlacement feature gate.
```

### Comment by [@mwysokin](https://github.com/mwysokin) — 2025-11-05T18:06:42Z

@pajakd  Quick question about using the behavior. The descriptions says that when we enable the feature flag we're going to use Balanced Placement for the preferred mode. I remember discussing at some point that it'd be great to use it also in the unconstrained mode so that this behavior becomes the default and even people not familiar with TAS who might not provide the label could use feature's benefits. And it'd also be useful in the required mode for example (sorry for my bias toward GKE) if I require that my workload fits within a block (in GKE it's one level above a rack) it could also be beneficial because multiple NVLDs might be involved. So why not use it everywhere?

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-11-06T07:58:50Z

I'm not sure yet why we don't support unconstrained and required, but the PR is already massive XXL, so if supporting the new annotations is non-trivial, then I would suggest a follow up PR for the ease of reviewing, and to basically reduce risk of numerous bugs.

EDIT: assuming support for unconstained and required is not bringing new API we could also cherrypick it to 0.15.1, because the code would be under alpha feature gate.

### Comment by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) — 2025-11-06T09:40:42Z

@mwysokin we can definitely think about how to incorporate `required` and `unconstrained` into the balanced TAS. 

The idea of using the `preferred` is that we need a way to mark a specific level of topology on which we perform the balancing. I might be wrong but I think that the `preferred` should cover all the use-cases we had so far.

### Comment by [@mwysokin](https://github.com/mwysokin) — 2025-11-06T14:12:21Z

I wouldn't block this PR from being merged just because there's no support for `required` and `unconstrained`. I do think though that it'd be quite beneficial long-term so I'd do a quick follow-up. Maybe we could have someone from AWS and Azure chime-in what the default behavior should be for unconstrained? We'll need to make assumptions about what is the level where the balancing happens, we know that for GKE the topology is block/rack/host/node. If AWS, Azure, Oracle and OpenShift have similar structures maybe we could always assume that we're balancing at 3rd from the bottom (racks) if not level is provided like in `unconstrained`.

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-11-12T12:46:09Z

What is the algorithmic complexity of the balanced placement in relation to BestFit, at least in some simplified cases. Do we expect increased performance might be a drawback? 

Knowing that could influence the decision if this should be default mode or the drawbacks are so big that it should be explicitly opted in

EDIT: it is not a blocker for Alpha. just would like to know going forward

### Comment by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) — 2025-11-12T14:49:31Z

> What is the algorithmic complexity of the balanced placement in relation to BestFit, at least in some simplified cases. Do we expect increased performance might be a drawback?
> 
> Knowing that could influence the decision if this should be default mode or the drawbacks are so big that it should be explicitly opted in
> 
> EDIT: it is not a blocker for Alpha. just would like to know going forward

The main component in the complexity of Balanced placement is something like

(max # racks in a block)^2 * (# slices to place)

if we balance on "rack" level.

The complexity of BestFit is (unless I'm missing something) linear everywhere. So, there might be some increase in complexity but I don't think it will be too much -- especially that this feature is designed for a special hardware.

### Comment by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2025-11-13T06:47:54Z

Thank you 👍 
/lgtm
/approve

I think the remaining comments are non-blocking:
- the potential refactoring https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/6851#discussion_r2519225966 is nice-to-have. In any case the impact will be easier to judge in a new diff (PR).
-  https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/6851#discussion_r2518896856 is just a small follow up.

We also need to improve the release-note, so that a user get a feeling of how it works, and why to enable it.

### Review by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) (commented) — 2025-10-02T13:09:52Z

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:1183** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-10-02T13:09:51Z
```diff
@@ -1153,6 +1154,43 @@ to ungate a Pod. The expectation is fulfilled if the Pod is observed as ungated
 or the ungating request fails. We hold ungating if there are pending ungatings
 within the PodSet.
 
+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assinged to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
+request must fit within a single domain on level L-1 and otherwise we fallback to the standard algorithm. The above
+assumptions are motivated by the application of the balanced placement algorithm to all-to-all communication
+on the specific networking for GPUs, but if the concept of balanced placement would be useful in other contexts it
+would be possible to lift these assumptions. This balancing algorithm is enabled by the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate.
+
+The algorithm could be summarized as follows:
+
+```
+1. For each domain on level L-1:
+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain
+ - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.
+2. If no domain on level L-1 fits the entire request, fallback to the standard algorithm.
+3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that maximizes the value of T.
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On levels L and L+1 find an optimal subset of ancestors of D that fit the request:
```

  ancestors -> descendants? \
  (At least, the code calls them `grandchildren`)

+cross-domain traffic.

+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the

+would be possible to lift these assumptions. This balancing algorithm is enabled by the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate.

+The algorithm could be summarized as follows:
+
+```
+1. For each domain on level L-1:
+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain
+ - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.

+3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that maximizes the value of T.
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On levels L and L+1 find an optimal subset of descendants of D that fit the request:
+- first optmize the size of the subset
+- secondly optimize the total capacity of the subset
+6. For the subset on L+1, place the pods by first placing T pods on each domain, and then distribute the rest abritrarily.
+```
+
+The balancing algorithm will support the following features of TAS:
+
+ - Slices. Instead of assigning pods, the balancing algorithm will assign slices.
+ - Leader-worker set.
```

  ```suggestion
   - LeaderWorkerSet.
  ```
  Does it mean we don't support other types of jobs?

+5. On levels L and L+1 find an optimal subset of descendants of D that fit the request:
+- first optmize the size of the subset
+- secondly optimize the total capacity of the subset
+6. For the subset on L+1, place the pods by first placing T pods on each domain, and then distribute the rest abritrarily.
+```
+
+The balancing algorithm will support the following features of TAS:
+
+ - Slices. Instead of assigning pods, the balancing algorithm will assign slices.
+ - Leader-worker set.
```

  It will support all the job types. I highlighted Jobset and LeaderWorkerSet because it required some work for the balanced placement to work with these.

+package scheduler

+import (
+	"maps"
+	"math"
+	"slices"

+
+func simulateGreedy(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32) (bool, int32, *domain, *domain) {
+	var selectedDomainsCount int32
+	var remainingSorted, sorted []*domain
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	remainingSliceCount := sliceCount
+	remainingLeaderCount := leaderCount
+	idx := 0
+	if leaderCount > 0 {
+		sorted = sortedDomainsWithLeader(domains, false)
+		for ; remainingLeaderCount > 0 && idx < len(sorted) && sorted[idx].leaderState > 0; idx++ {
+			selectedDomainsCount++
+			lastDomainWithLeader = sorted[idx]
+			remainingLeaderCount -= sorted[idx].leaderState
+			remainingSliceCount -= sorted[idx].sliceStateWithLeader
+		}
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(sorted[idx:], false)
+	} else {
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(domains, false)
+	}
+
+	if remainingLeaderCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+
+	for idx = 0; remainingSliceCount > 0 && idx < len(remainingSorted) && remainingSorted[idx].sliceState > 0; idx++ {
+		selectedDomainsCount++
+		lastDomain = remainingSorted[idx]
+		remainingSliceCount -= remainingSorted[idx].sliceState
+	}
+	if remainingSliceCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+	return true, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain
+}
+
+// The balance threshold value is maximum possible minimum number of slices placed on a domain in a balanced placement solution.
+// To find this value, we greedily pick the domains (starting from the largest one) to accommodate the request and simulate placing
+// the requested pods evenly on the selected domains.
+func balanceThresholdValue(startingDomain *domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, balanceOnChildren bool) (int32, bool) {
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
```

  Can this line be removed?
  These vars will be anyway `:=`-defined when calling `simulateGreedy()`.

+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assinged to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
```

  And what if the user uses `required`?
  
  For now, your answer (consistently in this PR) is that we fall back to BestFit. And maybe it's OK given the current use cases. Though in my feeling this makes BalancedProfile behave in a surprising way.
  
  I understand supporting this might be heavy in terms of code changes, so I won't suggest this too strongly. But I'm still curious about others' thoughts.

  I find the names of domain-related variables a bit confusing. For example:
  - I'd assume `levelDomains` are at level L, `lowerLevelDomains` are at level L+1 - but in fact it's L-1 & L, respectively.
  - Looking at `domains` vs. `levelDomains`, I'd guess the latter restricts the former by level - but it's rather just a type conversion.
  - `bestSingleDomain` is on level L-1; `currFitDomain` is an array on level L - also not obvious.
  
  I'd propose the following:
  
  - inline `domains` into the definition of `levelDomains` (which seems its only usage)
  - rename `currFitDomain` -> `currFitDomains`
  - use a consistent terminology (also related to L). Some ideas:
    (I mean to pick one scheme, not to mix them :)
    - for L :`requestedLevel...` / `levelL...`
    - for L-1: `parentLevel...` / `higherLevel...` / `levelUp...`
    - for L+1: `lowerLevel...` / `levelDown...`
      (here I'd avoid `childLevel` to avoid confusion between children & grandchildren, when looking from the L-1 perspective)
  
  WDYT?

- **pkg/cache/scheduler/tas_flavor_snapshot.go:758** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-10-29T09:39:17Z
```diff
@@ -741,28 +741,70 @@ func (s *TASFlavorSnapshot) findTopologyAssignment(
 
 	// phase 2a: determine the level at which the assignment is done along with
 	// the domains which can accommodate all pods/slices
-	fitLevelIdx, currFitDomain, reason := s.findLevelWithFitDomains(levelIdx, required, count, leaderCount, sliceSize, unconstrained)
-	if len(reason) > 0 {
-		return nil, reason
+	var currFitDomain []*domain
+	var bestSingleDomain *domain
+	var fitLevelIdx int
+	var useBalancedPlacement bool
+	var bestThreshold, bestLowerLevelDomainCount int32
+	if features.Enabled(features.TASBalancedPlacement) && !required && !unconstrained && levelIdx >= 1 {
+		// check if balanced placement is possible: look one level above the preferred level
+		// see if any (single) domain on that level fits the request and compute for each of
+		// them the balance threshold value
+		domains := s.domainsPerLevel[levelIdx-1]
+		levelDomains := slices.Collect(maps.Values(domains))
+		sliceCount := count / sliceSize
+		for _, levelDomain := range levelDomains {
+			threshold, fits := balanceThresholdValue(levelDomain, sliceCount, leaderCount, levelIdx == sliceLevelIdx)
+			_, lowerLevelDomainCount, _, _ := simulateGreedy(levelDomain.children, sliceCount, leaderCount)
```

  I'm concerned that this `lowerLevelDomainCount` is computed with _disregard_ of the `threshold` determined just above. (And generally, with disregard of balancing per-grandchildren).
  
  ---
  
  For example, consider a tree of domains with the following capacities for slices (no leader involved):
  [[[10, 4, 4, 4], [5], [5]], [[5, 5], [5, 5]]]. And suppose we want to fit 20 slices. 
  (Levels = block / sub-block / rack. L = sub-block, the middle one). 
  And now:
  
  * For the first block ([[10, 4, 4, 4], [5], [5]]):
    - The call to `balanceThresholdValue` will sort all its grandchildren into [10, 5, 5, 5, 4, 4, 4] and from that pick [10, 5, 5, 0, ...], returning 5 as `threshold`.
      Going back to original tree, this means [10, 0, 0, 0], [5], [5], i.e. taking _three_ sub-racks.
    - However, the call to `simulateGreedy` here will consider just children, i.e. [22, 5, 5], and claim that [20, 0, 0] is fine, i.e. that _one_ sub-rack is enough.
    - In the end, an impossible combination of (`threshold` = 5, `lowerLevelDomainCount` = 1) will "participate in the contest" below.
  * For the second sub-block ([[5, 5], [5, 5]]), it is actually possible to have (`threshold` = 5, `lLDC` = 2) - but this will lose the contest to (5, 1) from the previous sub-block.
  
  As a result, the current code will choose the first sub-block, which is actually not optimal.
  
  ---
  
  To get this right, I think we need to compute temporary _alternative capacity_ for a sub-block: "sum up all its racks but only those exceeding `threshold`". And then, run "greedy on sub-racks" with those.
  
  Or have I missed sth?

- **pkg/cache/scheduler/tas_flavor_snapshot.go:1485** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-10-29T10:47:42Z

 }
 
+func (d *domain) grandchildren() []*domain {
+	var size int
+	for _, c := range d.children {
+		size += len(c.children)
+	}
+	grandchildren := make([]*domain, 0, size)
+	for _, child := range d.children {
+		grandchildren = append(grandchildren, child.children...)
+	}
+	return grandchildren
+}
+
+func clearState(d *domain) {
+	d.state = int32(0)
+	d.sliceState = int32(0)
+	d.stateWithLeader = int32(0)
+	d.sliceStateWithLeader = int32(0)
+	d.leaderState = int32(0)
+	for _, child := range d.children {
+		clearState(child)
+	}
+}
+
+func (s *TASFlavorSnapshot) pruneDomainsBelowThreshold(root *domain, threshold int32, sliceSize int32, sliceLevelIdx int, level int) {
+	for _, d := range root.grandchildren() {
+		if d.sliceStateWithLeader < threshold {
```

  What if:
  - `d.sliceStateWithLeader < threshold`
  - `d.sliceState > threshold`
  - leader would be placed somewhere else?
  
  AFAIU this code will prune such location while it shouldn't?

- **pkg/cache/scheduler/tas_balanced_placement.go:96** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-10-29T11:20:45Z

@@ -0,0 +1,269 @@
+/*

+
+Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the "License");

+You may obtain a copy of the License at

+
+package scheduler
+
+import (
+	"maps"
+	"math"
+	"slices"
+)
+
+func simulateGreedy(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32) (bool, int32, *domain, *domain) {
+	var selectedDomainsCount int32
+	var remainingSorted, sorted []*domain
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	remainingSliceCount := sliceCount
+	remainingLeaderCount := leaderCount
+	idx := 0
+	if leaderCount > 0 {
+		sorted = sortedDomainsWithLeader(domains, false)
+		for ; remainingLeaderCount > 0 && idx < len(sorted) && sorted[idx].leaderState > 0; idx++ {
+			selectedDomainsCount++
+			lastDomainWithLeader = sorted[idx]
+			remainingLeaderCount -= sorted[idx].leaderState
+			remainingSliceCount -= sorted[idx].sliceStateWithLeader
+		}
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(sorted[idx:], false)
+	} else {
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(domains, false)
+	}
+
+	if remainingLeaderCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+
+	for idx = 0; remainingSliceCount > 0 && idx < len(remainingSorted) && remainingSorted[idx].sliceState > 0; idx++ {
+		selectedDomainsCount++
+		lastDomain = remainingSorted[idx]
+		remainingSliceCount -= remainingSorted[idx].sliceState
+	}
+	if remainingSliceCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+	return true, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain
+}
+
+// The balance threshold value is maximum possible minimum number of slices placed on a domain in a balanced placement solution.
+// To find this value, we greedily pick the domains (starting from the largest one) to accommodate the request and simulate placing
+// the requested pods evenly on the selected domains.
+func balanceThresholdValue(startingDomain *domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, balanceOnChildren bool) (int32, bool) {
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	var domainsToBalance []*domain
+	if sliceCount == 0 && leaderCount == 0 {
+		return 0, true
+	}
+	if startingDomain.sliceStateWithLeader < sliceCount || startingDomain.leaderState < leaderCount {
+		return 0, false
+	}
+	// verify if the request fits on this domain and return what is the threshold on the selected level
+	if balanceOnChildren {
+		domainsToBalance = startingDomain.children
+	} else {
+		domainsToBalance = startingDomain.grandchildren()
+	}
+
+	fits, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain := simulateGreedy(domainsToBalance, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+	if !fits {
+		return 0, false
+	}
+	threshold := sliceCount / selectedDomainsCount
+	if lastDomainWithLeader != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomainWithLeader.sliceStateWithLeader)
+	}
+	if lastDomain != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomain.sliceState)
+	}
+	return threshold, true
+}
+
+func selectOptimalDomainSetToFit(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, sliceSize int32, priorizeByEntropy bool) []*domain {
+	fit, optimalNumberOfDomains, _, _ := simulateGreedy(domains, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+	if !fit {
+		return nil
+	}
+
+	if priorizeByEntropy {
+		sortDomainsByCapacityAndEntropy(domains)
+	}
+
+	// domain_placements[i][j][k] stores a list of domains that uses 'i' domains with
```

  Nit: this is explanation is generally nice - but in 1 way ambiguous:
  
  A. "use (`i` domains with `j` leaders) and (`k` pods left to fit)
  B. "use `i` domains with ((`j` leaders and `k` pods) left to fit)
  
  It's not "abstract mean creativity"; I originally understood A (while I think you meant B).
  I think I fell into A due to reading left-to-right too impatiently.
  
  I'm not sure if it can be phrased more clearly and still nicely.
  How about just placing a pair of ( ) around "`j` leaders and `k` pods"?

+	"slices"

+func simulateGreedy(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32) (bool, int32, *domain, *domain) {
+	var selectedDomainsCount int32
+	var remainingSorted, sorted []*domain
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	remainingSliceCount := sliceCount
+	remainingLeaderCount := leaderCount
+	idx := 0
+	if leaderCount > 0 {
+		sorted = sortedDomainsWithLeader(domains, false)
+		for ; remainingLeaderCount > 0 && idx < len(sorted) && sorted[idx].leaderState > 0; idx++ {
+			selectedDomainsCount++
+			lastDomainWithLeader = sorted[idx]
+			remainingLeaderCount -= sorted[idx].leaderState
+			remainingSliceCount -= sorted[idx].sliceStateWithLeader
+		}
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(sorted[idx:], false)
+	} else {
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(domains, false)
+	}
+
+	if remainingLeaderCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+
+	for idx = 0; remainingSliceCount > 0 && idx < len(remainingSorted) && remainingSorted[idx].sliceState > 0; idx++ {
+		selectedDomainsCount++
+		lastDomain = remainingSorted[idx]
+		remainingSliceCount -= remainingSorted[idx].sliceState
+	}
+	if remainingSliceCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+	return true, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain
+}
+
+// The balance threshold value is maximum possible minimum number of slices placed on a domain in a balanced placement solution.
+// To find this value, we greedily pick the domains (starting from the largest one) to accommodate the request and simulate placing
+// the requested pods evenly on the selected domains.
+func balanceThresholdValue(startingDomain *domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, balanceOnChildren bool) (int32, bool) {
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	var domainsToBalance []*domain
+	if sliceCount == 0 && leaderCount == 0 {
+		return 0, true
+	}
+	if startingDomain.sliceStateWithLeader < sliceCount || startingDomain.leaderState < leaderCount {
+		return 0, false
+	}
+	// verify if the request fits on this domain and return what is the threshold on the selected level
+	if balanceOnChildren {
+		domainsToBalance = startingDomain.children
+	} else {
+		domainsToBalance = startingDomain.grandchildren()
+	}
+
+	fits, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain := simulateGreedy(domainsToBalance, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+	if !fits {
+		return 0, false
+	}
+	threshold := sliceCount / selectedDomainsCount
+	if lastDomainWithLeader != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomainWithLeader.sliceStateWithLeader)
+	}
+	if lastDomain != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomain.sliceState)
+	}
+	return threshold, true
+}
+
+func selectOptimalDomainSetToFit(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, sliceSize int32, priorizeByEntropy bool) []*domain {
+	fit, optimalNumberOfDomains, _, _ := simulateGreedy(domains, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+	if !fit {
+		return nil
+	}
+
+	if priorizeByEntropy {
+		sortDomainsByCapacityAndEntropy(domains)
+	}
+
+	// domain_placements[i][j][k] stores a list of domains that uses 'i' domains with
+	// 'j' leaders and 'k' pods left to fit
+	domainPlacements := make([]map[int32]map[int32][]*domain, optimalNumberOfDomains+1)
+	for i := range domainPlacements {
+		domainPlacements[i] = make(map[int32]map[int32][]*domain)
+	}
+	domainPlacements[0][leaderCount] = map[int32][]*domain{sliceCount * sliceSize: {}}
+
+	for _, d := range domains {
+		for i := optimalNumberOfDomains; i > 0; i-- {
+			for _, beforeLeader := range slices.Sorted(maps.Keys(domainPlacements[i-1])) {
+				for _, beforeState := range slices.Sorted(maps.Keys(domainPlacements[i-1][beforeLeader])) {
+					beforePlacement := domainPlacements[i-1][beforeLeader][beforeState]
+					if beforeLeader <= 0 && beforeState <= 0 {
+						continue
+					}
+					newPlacement := make([]*domain, len(beforePlacement), len(beforePlacement)+1)
+					copy(newPlacement, beforePlacement)
+					newPlacement = append(newPlacement, d)
+					// Case 1: Pick this domain with leader
+					if beforeLeader > 0 && d.leaderState > 0 {
+						afterLeader := beforeLeader - d.leaderState
+						afterState := beforeState - d.stateWithLeader
+						if domainPlacements[i][afterLeader] == nil {
+							domainPlacements[i][afterLeader] = make(map[int32][]*domain)
+						}
+						if _, alreadyThere := domainPlacements[i][afterLeader][afterState]; !alreadyThere {
+							domainPlacements[i][afterLeader][afterState] = newPlacement
+						}
+					}
+					// Case 2: Pick this domain without leader
+					if d.sliceState > 0 {
+						afterState := beforeState - d.state
+						if domainPlacements[i][beforeLeader] == nil {
+							domainPlacements[i][beforeLeader] = make(map[int32][]*domain)
+						}
+						if _, alreadyThere := domainPlacements[i][beforeLeader][afterState]; !alreadyThere {
+							domainPlacements[i][beforeLeader][afterState] = newPlacement
+						}
+					}
+				}
+			}
+		}
+	}
+
+	bestLeader := int32(-1 << 31) // minus infinity
+	var bestLeaderPlacement map[int32][]*domain
+
+	for j := range slices.Sorted(maps.Keys(domainPlacements[optimalNumberOfDomains])) {
```

  I'm not sure about the purpose of this loop.
  It seems that, currently, the only possible values of `leadersLeft` are 0 and 1.
  (And if this code is meant to support multiple leaders in the future, then I think we'd also need changes in various other places to support that fully).
  
  So, here, I'd suggest skipping this loop entirely & just taking
  `[domainPlacements][optimalNumberOfDomains][0]`.

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:1211** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-10-29T11:49:45Z
```diff
@@ -1173,6 +1179,46 @@ to ungate a Pod. The expectation is fulfilled if the Pod is observed as ungated
 or the ungating request fails. We hold ungating if there are pending ungatings
 within the PodSet.
 
+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assinged to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
+request must fit within a single domain on level L-1 and otherwise we fallback to the standard algorithm. The above
+assumptions are motivated by the application of the balanced placement algorithm to all-to-all communication
+on the specific networking for GPUs. If the concept of balanced placement would be useful in other contexts it
+would be possible to lift these assumptions. This balancing algorithm is enabled by the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate.
+
+The algorithm could be summarized as follows:
+
+```
+1. For each domain on level L-1:
+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain
+ - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.
+2. If no domain on level L-1 fits the entire request, fallback to the standard algorithm.
+3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that 
+- first maximizes the value of T
+- secondly minimizes the number of domains that need to be used on level L to fit the request 
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On levels L and L+1 find an optimal subset of descendants of D that fit the request:
+- first optmize the size of the subset
```

  Oh, but this happens separately on both levels. So, strictly speaking, you optimize (in order) for:
  
  1. Least number of domains on level L
  2. Least total capacity of those domains
  3. Picking single domains on level L according to highest entropy of their children capacities
  4. Least number of domains on level L+1 (within the chosen domains on level L)
  5. Least total capacity of those domains
  
  Specifically, you call `selectOptimalDomainSetToFit` twice (first from the main function, then from `placeSlicesOnDomainsBalanced`); the first call takes care for # 1-3, the second for # 4-5.
  
  Am I right?
  
  ---
  
  BTW when you say "optimize the total capacity", I'd suggest specifying in which direction.
  (Given that we already employ "least free" & "most free" in various contexts - it can be unclear).

+				bestThreshold = threshold
+				bestLowerLevelDomainCount = lowerLevelDomainCount
+				bestSingleDomain = levelDomain

+		}

+			s.pruneDomainsBelowThreshold(bestSingleDomain, bestThreshold, sliceSize, sliceLevelIdx, levelIdx-1)
+			// the balanced placement algorithm selects domains on three levels: levelIdx -1, levelIdx and levelIdx + 1
+			// unless levelIdx == sliceLevelIdx in which case it selects only on two levels: levelIdx -1 and levelIdx
+			if levelIdx < sliceLevelIdx {

```

  Here the last param is `true`, so we prioritize by entropy. (IIUC this amounts to priority "# 3" in one of my comments above).
  
  Out of curiosity - what is the purpose of this entropy part?
  
  For example: If we want to assign 20 pods to [[[12, 10]], [[11, 11]]], then IIUC the entropy sorter will prioritize [11, 11] (binary entropy 1.0) over [12, 10] (binary entropy 0.994), and as a result the algorithm will pick the two [11, 11] over [12, 10] (which it would likely choose with `prioritizeByEntropy == false`).
  But this looks like increasing fragmentation rather than decreasing it - so is it desired?

+	remainingLeaderCount := leaderCount

+	}

### Review by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) (commented) — 2025-10-29T14:08:51Z

- **pkg/cache/scheduler/tas_balanced_placement.go:96** by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) — 2025-10-29T14:08:51Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,269 @@
+/*
+Copyright The Kubernetes Authors.
+
+Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the "License");
+you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.
+You may obtain a copy of the License at
+
+    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0
+
+Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software
+distributed under the License is distributed on an "AS IS" BASIS,
+WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.
+See the License for the specific language governing permissions and
+limitations under the License.
+*/
+
+package scheduler
+
+import (
+	"maps"
+	"math"
+	"slices"
+)
+
+func simulateGreedy(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32) (bool, int32, *domain, *domain) {
+	var selectedDomainsCount int32
+	var remainingSorted, sorted []*domain
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	remainingSliceCount := sliceCount
+	remainingLeaderCount := leaderCount
+	idx := 0
+	if leaderCount > 0 {
+		sorted = sortedDomainsWithLeader(domains, false)
+		for ; remainingLeaderCount > 0 && idx < len(sorted) && sorted[idx].leaderState > 0; idx++ {
+			selectedDomainsCount++
+			lastDomainWithLeader = sorted[idx]
+			remainingLeaderCount -= sorted[idx].leaderState
+			remainingSliceCount -= sorted[idx].sliceStateWithLeader
+		}
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(sorted[idx:], false)
+	} else {
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(domains, false)
+	}
+
+	if remainingLeaderCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+
+	for idx = 0; remainingSliceCount > 0 && idx < len(remainingSorted) && remainingSorted[idx].sliceState > 0; idx++ {
+		selectedDomainsCount++
+		lastDomain = remainingSorted[idx]
+		remainingSliceCount -= remainingSorted[idx].sliceState
+	}
+	if remainingSliceCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+	return true, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain
+}
+
+// The balance threshold value is maximum possible minimum number of slices placed on a domain in a balanced placement solution.
+// To find this value, we greedily pick the domains (starting from the largest one) to accommodate the request and simulate placing
+// the requested pods evenly on the selected domains.
+func balanceThresholdValue(startingDomain *domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, balanceOnChildren bool) (int32, bool) {
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	var domainsToBalance []*domain
+	if sliceCount == 0 && leaderCount == 0 {
+		return 0, true
+	}
+	if startingDomain.sliceStateWithLeader < sliceCount || startingDomain.leaderState < leaderCount {
+		return 0, false
+	}
+	// verify if the request fits on this domain and return what is the threshold on the selected level
+	if balanceOnChildren {
+		domainsToBalance = startingDomain.children
+	} else {
+		domainsToBalance = startingDomain.grandchildren()
+	}
+
+	fits, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain := simulateGreedy(domainsToBalance, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+	if !fits {
+		return 0, false
+	}
+	threshold := sliceCount / selectedDomainsCount
+	if lastDomainWithLeader != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomainWithLeader.sliceStateWithLeader)
+	}
+	if lastDomain != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomain.sliceState)
+	}
+	return threshold, true
+}
+
+func selectOptimalDomainSetToFit(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, sliceSize int32, priorizeByEntropy bool) []*domain {
+	fit, optimalNumberOfDomains, _, _ := simulateGreedy(domains, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+	if !fit {
+		return nil
+	}
+
+	if priorizeByEntropy {
+		sortDomainsByCapacityAndEntropy(domains)
+	}
+
+	// domain_placements[i][j][k] stores a list of domains that uses 'i' domains with
```

  Updated the description. Also updated `k pods` to `k workers`. Bc leaders are pods too. But this might actually cause more confusion as LeaderWorkerSet is only one of the types of jobs we support.

+			// unless levelIdx == sliceLevelIdx in which case it selects only on two levels: levelIdx -1 and levelIdx
+			if levelIdx < sliceLevelIdx {
+				currFitDomain = selectOptimalDomainSetToFit(bestSingleDomain.children, sliceCount, leaderCount, sliceSize, true)
```

  Good point. The assumption when proposing the entropy was that when choosing the domain with capacities [c_1,...] we will place min c_i pods on each sub-domain. 
  
  I'll think if there is a way to improve it (keeping in mind that the entropy is only a tie-breaker and should not influence the overall algorithm too much).

### Review by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) (commented) — 2025-10-30T07:51:25Z

- **pkg/cache/scheduler/tas_flavor_snapshot.go:773** by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) — 2025-10-30T07:51:24Z
```diff
@@ -741,28 +741,70 @@ func (s *TASFlavorSnapshot) findTopologyAssignment(
 
 	// phase 2a: determine the level at which the assignment is done along with
 	// the domains which can accommodate all pods/slices
-	fitLevelIdx, currFitDomain, reason := s.findLevelWithFitDomains(levelIdx, required, count, leaderCount, sliceSize, unconstrained)
-	if len(reason) > 0 {
-		return nil, reason
+	var currFitDomain []*domain
+	var bestSingleDomain *domain
+	var fitLevelIdx int
+	var useBalancedPlacement bool
+	var bestThreshold, bestLowerLevelDomainCount int32
+	if features.Enabled(features.TASBalancedPlacement) && !required && !unconstrained && levelIdx >= 1 {
+		// check if balanced placement is possible: look one level above the preferred level
+		// see if any (single) domain on that level fits the request and compute for each of
+		// them the balance threshold value
+		domains := s.domainsPerLevel[levelIdx-1]
+		levelDomains := slices.Collect(maps.Values(domains))
+		sliceCount := count / sliceSize
+		for _, levelDomain := range levelDomains {
+			threshold, fits := balanceThresholdValue(levelDomain, sliceCount, leaderCount, levelIdx == sliceLevelIdx)
+			_, lowerLevelDomainCount, _, _ := simulateGreedy(levelDomain.children, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+			if fits && (threshold > bestThreshold || (threshold == bestThreshold && lowerLevelDomainCount < bestLowerLevelDomainCount)) {
+				bestThreshold = threshold
+				bestLowerLevelDomainCount = lowerLevelDomainCount
+				bestSingleDomain = levelDomain
+				currFitDomain = []*domain{levelDomain}
+				useBalancedPlacement = true
+			}
+		}
+
+		if useBalancedPlacement {
+			s.pruneDomainsBelowThreshold(bestSingleDomain, bestThreshold, sliceSize, sliceLevelIdx, levelIdx-1)
+			// the balanced placement algorithm selects domains on three levels: levelIdx -1, levelIdx and levelIdx + 1
+			// unless levelIdx == sliceLevelIdx in which case it selects only on two levels: levelIdx -1 and levelIdx
+			if levelIdx < sliceLevelIdx {
+				currFitDomain = selectOptimalDomainSetToFit(bestSingleDomain.children, sliceCount, leaderCount, sliceSize, true)
```

  This function returns nil only if the request does not fit in the provided domains.
  
  But for the `bestSingleDomain` we (few lines above) call the `balanceThresholdValue` that checks that the request fits even if we only use domains of size at least the threshold value.
  
  So, if we are in this place in the code, it cannot return nil.

### Review by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) (commented) — 2025-10-30T08:37:06Z

- **pkg/cache/scheduler/tas_balanced_placement.go:151** by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) — 2025-10-30T08:37:06Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,269 @@
+/*
+Copyright The Kubernetes Authors.
+
+Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the "License");
+you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.
+You may obtain a copy of the License at

+See the License for the specific language governing permissions and

+package scheduler
+
+import (
+	"maps"
+	"math"
+	"slices"
+)
+
+func simulateGreedy(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32) (bool, int32, *domain, *domain) {
+	var selectedDomainsCount int32
+	var remainingSorted, sorted []*domain
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	remainingSliceCount := sliceCount
+	remainingLeaderCount := leaderCount
+	idx := 0
+	if leaderCount > 0 {
+		sorted = sortedDomainsWithLeader(domains, false)
+		for ; remainingLeaderCount > 0 && idx < len(sorted) && sorted[idx].leaderState > 0; idx++ {
+			selectedDomainsCount++
+			lastDomainWithLeader = sorted[idx]
+			remainingLeaderCount -= sorted[idx].leaderState
+			remainingSliceCount -= sorted[idx].sliceStateWithLeader
+		}
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(sorted[idx:], false)
+	} else {
+		remainingSorted = sortedDomains(domains, false)
+	}
+
+	if remainingLeaderCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+
+	for idx = 0; remainingSliceCount > 0 && idx < len(remainingSorted) && remainingSorted[idx].sliceState > 0; idx++ {
+		selectedDomainsCount++
+		lastDomain = remainingSorted[idx]
+		remainingSliceCount -= remainingSorted[idx].sliceState
+	}
+	if remainingSliceCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+	return true, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain
+}
+
+// The balance threshold value is maximum possible minimum number of slices placed on a domain in a balanced placement solution.
+// To find this value, we greedily pick the domains (starting from the largest one) to accommodate the request and simulate placing
+// the requested pods evenly on the selected domains.
+func balanceThresholdValue(startingDomain *domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, balanceOnChildren bool) (int32, bool) {
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	var domainsToBalance []*domain
+	if sliceCount == 0 && leaderCount == 0 {
+		return 0, true
+	}
+	if startingDomain.sliceStateWithLeader < sliceCount || startingDomain.leaderState < leaderCount {
+		return 0, false
+	}
+	// verify if the request fits on this domain and return what is the threshold on the selected level
+	if balanceOnChildren {
+		domainsToBalance = startingDomain.children
+	} else {
+		domainsToBalance = startingDomain.grandchildren()
+	}
+
+	fits, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain := simulateGreedy(domainsToBalance, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+	if !fits {
+		return 0, false
+	}
+	threshold := sliceCount / selectedDomainsCount
+	if lastDomainWithLeader != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomainWithLeader.sliceStateWithLeader)
+	}
+	if lastDomain != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomain.sliceState)
+	}
+	return threshold, true
+}
+
+func selectOptimalDomainSetToFit(domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32, sliceSize int32, priorizeByEntropy bool) []*domain {
+	fit, optimalNumberOfDomains, _, _ := simulateGreedy(domains, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+	if !fit {
+		return nil
+	}
+
+	if priorizeByEntropy {
+		sortDomainsByCapacityAndEntropy(domains)
+	}
+
+	// domain_placements[i][j][k] stores a list of domains that uses 'i' domains with
+	// 'j' leaders and 'k' pods left to fit
+	domainPlacements := make([]map[int32]map[int32][]*domain, optimalNumberOfDomains+1)
+	for i := range domainPlacements {
+		domainPlacements[i] = make(map[int32]map[int32][]*domain)
+	}
+	domainPlacements[0][leaderCount] = map[int32][]*domain{sliceCount * sliceSize: {}}
+
+	for _, d := range domains {
+		for i := optimalNumberOfDomains; i > 0; i-- {
+			for _, beforeLeader := range slices.Sorted(maps.Keys(domainPlacements[i-1])) {
+				for _, beforeState := range slices.Sorted(maps.Keys(domainPlacements[i-1][beforeLeader])) {
+					beforePlacement := domainPlacements[i-1][beforeLeader][beforeState]
+					if beforeLeader <= 0 && beforeState <= 0 {
+						continue
+					}
+					newPlacement := make([]*domain, len(beforePlacement), len(beforePlacement)+1)
+					copy(newPlacement, beforePlacement)
+					newPlacement = append(newPlacement, d)
+					// Case 1: Pick this domain with leader
+					if beforeLeader > 0 && d.leaderState > 0 {
+						afterLeader := beforeLeader - d.leaderState
+						afterState := beforeState - d.stateWithLeader
+						if domainPlacements[i][afterLeader] == nil {
+							domainPlacements[i][afterLeader] = make(map[int32][]*domain)
+						}
+						if _, alreadyThere := domainPlacements[i][afterLeader][afterState]; !alreadyThere {
+							domainPlacements[i][afterLeader][afterState] = newPlacement
+						}
+					}
+					// Case 2: Pick this domain without leader
+					if d.sliceState > 0 {
+						afterState := beforeState - d.state
+						if domainPlacements[i][beforeLeader] == nil {
+							domainPlacements[i][beforeLeader] = make(map[int32][]*domain)
+						}
+						if _, alreadyThere := domainPlacements[i][beforeLeader][afterState]; !alreadyThere {
+							domainPlacements[i][beforeLeader][afterState] = newPlacement
+						}
+					}
+				}
+			}
+		}
+	}
+
+	bestLeader := int32(-1 << 31) // minus infinity
+	var bestLeaderPlacement map[int32][]*domain
+
+	for j := range slices.Sorted(maps.Keys(domainPlacements[optimalNumberOfDomains])) {
```

  Right, done.

### Review by [@PBundyra](https://github.com/PBundyra) (commented) — 2025-10-30T14:48:35Z

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:1226** by [@PBundyra](https://github.com/PBundyra) — 2025-10-30T14:48:35Z
```diff
@@ -1173,6 +1179,46 @@ to ungate a Pod. The expectation is fulfilled if the Pod is observed as ungated
 or the ungating request fails. We hold ungating if there are pending ungatings
 within the PodSet.
 
+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assigned to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
+request must fit within a single domain on level L-1 and otherwise we fallback to the standard algorithm. The above
+assumptions are motivated by the application of the balanced placement algorithm to all-to-all communication
+on the specific networking for GPUs. If the concept of balanced placement would be useful in other contexts it
+would be possible to lift these assumptions. This balancing algorithm is enabled by the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate.
+
+The algorithm could be summarized as follows:
+
+```
+1. For each domain on level L-1:
+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain
+ - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.
+2. If no domain on level L-1 fits the entire request, fallback to the standard algorithm.
+3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that 
+- first maximizes the value of T
+- secondly minimizes the number of domains that need to be used on level L to fit the request 
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On levels L and L+1 find an optimal subset of descendants of D that fit the request:
+- first optmize the size of the subset
+- secondly optimize the total capacity of the subset
+6. For the subset on L+1, place the pods by first placing T pods on each domain, and then distribute the rest abritrarily.
+```
+
+The balancing algorithm will support all the job types currently supported by TAS including:
+
+ - JobSet. Instead of assigning pods, the balancing algorithm will assign slices.
+ - LeaderWorkerSet. Will co-locate leader with workers while keeping the overall
+ assignment per node balanced.
+
```

  Could we add some examples on how this works for 3-level topology (block/rack/hostname)?

  This makes sense and I think it is required. Added a code and a test.

  IIUC this function does two things:
  1) Checks if the whole request can be accommodated in this parent domain
  2) Calculates the optimal "T" value
  
  Can we separate those two responsibilities into two separate function, and skip parent domains that can accommodate the whole request right away?

### Review by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) (commented) — 2025-10-30T19:09:25Z

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:1211** by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) — 2025-10-30T19:09:24Z
```diff
@@ -1173,6 +1179,46 @@ to ungate a Pod. The expectation is fulfilled if the Pod is observed as ungated
 or the ungating request fails. We hold ungating if there are pending ungatings
 within the PodSet.
 
+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assinged to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
+request must fit within a single domain on level L-1 and otherwise we fallback to the standard algorithm. The above
+assumptions are motivated by the application of the balanced placement algorithm to all-to-all communication
+on the specific networking for GPUs. If the concept of balanced placement would be useful in other contexts it
+would be possible to lift these assumptions. This balancing algorithm is enabled by the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate.
+
+The algorithm could be summarized as follows:
+
+```
+1. For each domain on level L-1:
+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain
+ - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.
+2. If no domain on level L-1 fits the entire request, fallback to the standard algorithm.
+3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that 
+- first maximizes the value of T
+- secondly minimizes the number of domains that need to be used on level L to fit the request 
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On levels L and L+1 find an optimal subset of descendants of D that fit the request:
+- first optmize the size of the subset
```

  Done.

+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. +last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,

+cross-domain traffic.

+

+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain

+- first maximizes the value of T
+- secondly minimizes the number of domains that need to be used on level L to fit the request 
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On level L find an optimal subset of children of D that fit the request:
+- first minimize the size of the subset
+- secondly minimize the total capacity of the subset
+- thirdly minimize entropies of children capacities of the subset
```

  ```suggestion
  - thirdly maximize entropies of children capacities of the subset

+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assigned to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
+request must fit within a single domain on level L-1 and otherwise we fallback to the standard algorithm. The above
+assumptions are motivated by the application of the balanced placement algorithm to all-to-all communication
+on the specific networking for GPUs. If the concept of balanced placement would be useful in other contexts it
+would be possible to lift these assumptions. This balancing algorithm is enabled by the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate.
+
+The algorithm could be summarized as follows:
+
+```
+1. For each domain on level L-1:
+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain
+ - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.
+2. If no domain on level L-1 fits the entire request, fallback to the standard algorithm.
+3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that 
+- first maximizes the value of T
+- secondly minimizes the number of domains that need to be used on level L to fit the request 
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On levels L and L+1 find an optimal subset of descendants of D that fit the request:
+- first optmize the size of the subset
+- secondly optimize the total capacity of the subset
+6. For the subset on L+1, place the pods by first placing T pods on each domain, and then distribute the rest abritrarily.
+```
+
+The balancing algorithm will support all the job types currently supported by TAS including:
+
+ - JobSet. Instead of assigning pods, the balancing algorithm will assign slices.
+ - LeaderWorkerSet. Will co-locate leader with workers while keeping the overall
+ assignment per node balanced.
+
```

  > for 3-level topology (block/rack/hostname)?
  
  Nit: hostname, if included, must be [the only level](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/blob/50b8db0076113599288c911d126750b703516fb8/apis/kueue/v1beta1/workload_types.go#L199-L201) in a TAS assignment.
  So, if we want a realistic example, we could avoid "hostname".

### Review by [@pajakd](https://github.com/pajakd) (commented) — 2025-10-31T06:53:53Z

@@ -741,28 +741,70 @@ func (s *TASFlavorSnapshot) findTopologyAssignment(
 
 	// phase 2a: determine the level at which the assignment is done along with
 	// the domains which can accommodate all pods/slices
-	fitLevelIdx, currFitDomain, reason := s.findLevelWithFitDomains(levelIdx, required, count, leaderCount, sliceSize, unconstrained)
-	if len(reason) > 0 {
-		return nil, reason
+	var currFitDomain []*domain
+	var bestSingleDomain *domain
+	var fitLevelIdx int
+	var useBalancedPlacement bool
+	var bestThreshold, bestLowerLevelDomainCount int32
+	if features.Enabled(features.TASBalancedPlacement) && !required && !unconstrained && levelIdx >= 1 {
+		// check if balanced placement is possible: look one level above the preferred level
+		// see if any (single) domain on that level fits the request and compute for each of
+		// them the balance threshold value

+			_, lowerLevelDomainCount, _, _ := simulateGreedy(levelDomain.children, sliceCount, leaderCount)
+			if fits && (threshold > bestThreshold || (threshold == bestThreshold && lowerLevelDomainCount < bestLowerLevelDomainCount)) {
+				bestThreshold = threshold
+				bestLowerLevelDomainCount = lowerLevelDomainCount
+				bestSingleDomain = levelDomain
+				currFitDomain = []*domain{levelDomain}
+				useBalancedPlacement = true
+			}
+		}

+			s.pruneDomainsBelowThreshold(bestSingleDomain, bestThreshold, sliceSize, sliceLevelIdx, levelIdx-1)
+			// the balanced placement algorithm selects domains on three levels: levelIdx -1, levelIdx and levelIdx + 1
+			// unless levelIdx == sliceLevelIdx in which case it selects only on two levels: levelIdx -1 and levelIdx
+			if levelIdx < sliceLevelIdx {
+				currFitDomain = selectOptimalDomainSetToFit(bestSingleDomain.children, sliceCount, leaderCount, sliceSize, true)

+

+ - LeaderWorkerSet. Will co-locate leader with workers while keeping the overall
+ assignment per node balanced.
+
```

  Added a couple of examples.
  
  In the assignment TAS would output only data for the `hostname` level but the algorithm processes all the levels and we know where these `hostname` nodes are in the topology. So I think such examples are fine, no?

+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assinged to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
```

  For now I would prefer to leave it more restricted. We can always add support of `required` for the Balanced Placement in the future.

+func (d *domain) grandchildren() []*domain {
+	var size int
+	for _, c := range d.children {
+		size += len(c.children)
+	}
+	grandchildren := make([]*domain, 0, size)
+	for _, child := range d.children {
+		grandchildren = append(grandchildren, child.children...)
+	}
+	return grandchildren
+}
+
+func clearState(d *domain) {
+	d.state = int32(0)
+	d.sliceState = int32(0)
+	d.stateWithLeader = int32(0)
+	d.sliceStateWithLeader = int32(0)
+	d.leaderState = int32(0)
+	for _, child := range d.children {
+		clearState(child)
+	}
+}
+
+func (s *TASFlavorSnapshot) pruneDomainsBelowThreshold(root *domain, threshold int32, sliceSize int32, sliceLevelIdx int, level int) {
+	for _, d := range root.grandchildren() {
+		if d.sliceStateWithLeader < threshold {
```

  The threshold T is defined as "a domain must accommodate at least T slices even if the leader is placed there too" (see the balanceThresholdValue). So I think we don't prune any domain that should not be pruned. If any, the value of threshold is slightly lower because we leave "space" for the leader on every domain so we might prune too little.
  
  The algorithm could be slightly suboptimal for LeaderWorkerSet but I want to only provide basic support for LWS and I want to avoid making the alg more complex than it already is (especially that LWS is for now unlikely to be used together with Balanced Placement).

```

  I'm fine with picking a placement that is not best, especially in some corner cases (like, say, LWS).
  
  However, what concerns me here is that you might:
  - first select some high threshold (in `simulateGreedy`) based on a more accurate simualtion \
    (which takes into account that not every leader capacity is actually consumed by a leader)
  - then, when doing actual placement, prune a bit more aggressively and - as a result - no longer be able to allocate pods with the determined threshold T.
  
  Leading, in the worst case, to an error being thrown, not a suboptimal placement.
  
  WDYT?

### Review by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) (commented) — 2025-10-31T10:36:53Z

- **keps/2724-topology-aware-scheduling/README.md:1226** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-10-31T10:36:53Z
```diff
@@ -1173,6 +1179,46 @@ to ungate a Pod. The expectation is fulfilled if the Pod is observed as ungated
 or the ungating request fails. We hold ungating if there are pending ungatings
 within the PodSet.
 
+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assigned to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
+request must fit within a single domain on level L-1 and otherwise we fallback to the standard algorithm. The above
+assumptions are motivated by the application of the balanced placement algorithm to all-to-all communication
+on the specific networking for GPUs. If the concept of balanced placement would be useful in other contexts it
+would be possible to lift these assumptions. This balancing algorithm is enabled by the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate.
+
+The algorithm could be summarized as follows:
+
+```
+1. For each domain on level L-1:
+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain
+ - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.
+2. If no domain on level L-1 fits the entire request, fallback to the standard algorithm.
+3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that 
+- first maximizes the value of T
+- secondly minimizes the number of domains that need to be used on level L to fit the request 
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On levels L and L+1 find an optimal subset of descendants of D that fit the request:
+- first optmize the size of the subset
+- secondly optimize the total capacity of the subset
+6. For the subset on L+1, place the pods by first placing T pods on each domain, and then distribute the rest abritrarily.
+```
+
+The balancing algorithm will support all the job types currently supported by TAS including:
+
+ - JobSet. Instead of assigning pods, the balancing algorithm will assign slices.
+ - LeaderWorkerSet. Will co-locate leader with workers while keeping the overall
+ assignment per node balanced.
+
```

  Oh, :+1: , my apologies.

@@ -1173,6 +1180,62 @@ to ungate a Pod. The expectation is fulfilled if the Pod is observed as ungated
 or the ungating request fails. We hold ungating if there are pending ungatings
 within the PodSet.
 
+### Balanced placement
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria) and trying to pack as many pods as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods as evenly as possible across these domains. 
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assigned to the last considered domain (even though the existing algorithms choose the best possible
+last domain). For example 12 pods distributed among domains with capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However,
+in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be
+all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather) since more balanced placement leads to more efficient
+cross-domain traffic.
+
+In the first implemetation, we propose to perform the balanced algorithm only on two consequtive levels indicated
+by the user with the `preferred` flag. Let L be the level indicated by the `preferred` flag. We assume that the
+request must fit within a single domain on level L-1 and otherwise we fallback to the standard algorithm. The above
+assumptions are motivated by the application of the balanced placement algorithm to all-to-all communication
+on the specific networking for GPUs. If the concept of balanced placement would be useful in other contexts it
+would be possible to lift these assumptions. This balancing algorithm is enabled by the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate.
+
+The algorithm could be summarized as follows:
+
+```
+1. For each domain on level L-1:
+ - check if the entire request fits on this domain
+ - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.
+2. If no domain on level L-1 fits the entire request, fallback to the standard algorithm.
+3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that 
+- first maximizes the value of T
+- secondly minimizes the number of domains that need to be used on level L to fit the request 
+4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
+5. On level L find an optimal subset of children of D that fit the request:
+- first minimize the size of the subset
+- secondly minimize the total capacity of the subset
+- thirdly maximize entropies of children capacities of the subset
+6. On level L+1 find an optimal subset of children of domains from step 5 that fit the request:
+- first minimize the size of the subset
+- secondly minimize the total capacity of the subset
+7. For the subset found in step 6, place the pods by first placing T pods on each domain, and then distribute the rest abritrarily.
```

  (list formatting nit)
  
  ```suggestion
  1. For each domain on level L-1:
     - check if the entire request fits on this domain
     - calculate T, the maximum possible minimum number of pods that would be placed on a domain on level L+1 if the request is placed on this domain.
  2. If no domain on level L-1 fits the entire request, fallback to the standard algorithm.
  3. Otherwise, pick a domain D on level L-1 that 
     - first maximizes the value of T
     - secondly minimizes the number of domains that need to be used on level L to fit the request 
  4. Prune every descendant of D with capacity below T.
  5. On level L find an optimal subset of children of D that fit the request:
     - first minimize the size of the subset
     - secondly minimize the total capacity of the subset
     - thirdly maximize entropies of children capacities of the subset
  6. On level L+1 find an optimal subset of children of domains from step 5 that fit the request:
     - first minimize the size of the subset
     - secondly minimize the total capacity of the subset
  7. For the subset found in step 6, place the pods by first placing T pods on each domain, and then distribute the rest abritrarily.
  ```

- **pkg/cache/scheduler/tas_balanced_placement.go:77** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-10-31T14:29:33Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,291 @@
+/*
+Copyright The Kubernetes Authors.
+
+Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the "License");
+you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.
+You may obtain a copy of the License at
+
+    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0
+
+Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software
+distributed under the License is distributed on an "AS IS" BASIS,
+WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.
+See the License for the specific language governing permissions and
+limitations under the License.
+*/
+
+package scheduler
+
+import (
+	"maps"
+	"math"
+	"slices"
+)
+
+// evaluateGreedyAssignment simulates placement of a (leaderCount, sliceCount) request on the given domains.
+// It returns whether the request fits, how many domains greedy algorithm uses and what would be the last
+// used domain (with and without leader)
+func evaluateGreedyAssignment(s *TASFlavorSnapshot, domains []*domain, sliceCount int32, leaderCount int32) (bool, int32, *domain, *domain) {
+	var selectedDomainsCount int32
+	var sortedWithoutLeader, sortedWithLeader []*domain
+	var lastDomain, lastDomainWithLeader *domain
+	remainingSliceCount := sliceCount
+	remainingLeaderCount := leaderCount
+	idx := 0
+	if leaderCount > 0 {
+		sortedWithLeader = s.sortedDomainsWithLeader(domains, false)
+		for ; remainingLeaderCount > 0 && idx < len(sortedWithLeader) && sortedWithLeader[idx].leaderState > 0; idx++ {
+			selectedDomainsCount++
+			lastDomainWithLeader = sortedWithLeader[idx]
+			remainingLeaderCount -= sortedWithLeader[idx].leaderState
+			remainingSliceCount -= sortedWithLeader[idx].sliceStateWithLeader
+		}
+		sortedWithoutLeader = s.sortedDomains(sortedWithLeader[idx:], false)
+	} else {
+		sortedWithoutLeader = s.sortedDomains(domains, false)
+	}
+
+	if remainingLeaderCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+
+	for idx = 0; remainingSliceCount > 0 && idx < len(sortedWithoutLeader) && sortedWithoutLeader[idx].sliceState > 0; idx++ {
+		selectedDomainsCount++
+		lastDomain = sortedWithoutLeader[idx]
+		remainingSliceCount -= sortedWithoutLeader[idx].sliceState
+	}
+	if remainingSliceCount > 0 {
+		return false, 0, nil, nil
+	}
+	return true, selectedDomainsCount, lastDomainWithLeader, lastDomain
+}
+
+// The balance threshold value is maximum possible minimum number of slices placed on a domain in a balanced placement solution.
+func balanceThresholdValue(sliceCount int32, selectedDomainsCount int32, lastDomainWithLeader *domain, lastDomain *domain) int32 {
+	threshold := sliceCount / selectedDomainsCount
+	if lastDomainWithLeader != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomainWithLeader.sliceStateWithLeader)
+	}
+	if lastDomain != nil {
+		threshold = min(threshold, lastDomain.sliceStateWithLeader)
```

  I see, this is a fix against the "1+9 -> [1+5, 1+4]" problem.
  Though I think it deserves a comment. 
  
  Given how carefully you simulate (in `evaluateGreedyAssignment`, first sorting with leader, then sorting without, etc.), a subsequent reader of this code may wonder why we do `min(..., sliceStateWithLeader)` here? Why not just `min(..., sliceState)`?
  Someone could be even tempted to switch it - and fall back into the problem.
  (OK, I see you added a test, so a test would stop them - but I imagine I could lose 1+ hour on reflecting on this code, then testing such change, then tracking why that test failed, etc.)
  
  Ideally, you could create a follow-up GitHub issue (with a TODO linking to it inserted here) to switch this back to `.sliceState`, and address the problem on the pruning side (which I imagine would lead to slightly better balancing for LWS).
  BTW, while reimplementing pruning, we could also care for its reversibility, thus enabling fallback to BestFit in case there's any other problem here that we overlooked so far. So I'd mention that in the follow-up issue as well.
  
  WDYT?

- **site/content/en/docs/concepts/topology_aware_scheduling.md:264** by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2025-10-31T14:44:11Z
```diff
@@ -239,6 +239,34 @@ The following table summarizes the behavior based on the combination of the feat
 
 We recommend keeping all three feature gates enabled to ensure the fastest feedback loop for workloads affected by node failures.
 
+#### Balanced Placement
+{{< feature-state state="alpha" for_version="v0.15" >}}
+{{% alert title="Note" color="primary" %}}
+`TASBalancedPlacement` is currently an alpha feature and is disabled by default.
+
+You can enable it by editing the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate. Refer to the
+[Installation guide](/docs/installation/#change-the-feature-gates-configuration)
+for instructions on configuring feature gates.
+{{% /alert %}}
+
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of
+iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria)
+and trying to pack as many pods/slices as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the
+optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods/slices as evenly as possible across
+these domains.
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assigned to the last considered domain. For example 12 pods distributed among domains with
+capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However, in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would
+be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather)
+since more balanced placement leads to more efficient cross-domain traffic.
+
+To use this feature, use the `kueue.x-k8s.io/podset-preferred-topology` annotation on the Job. Kueue TAS make 
```

  ```suggestion
  To use this feature, use the `kueue.x-k8s.io/podset-preferred-topology` annotation on the Job. Kueue TAS makes 
  ```

 We recommend keeping all three feature gates enabled to ensure the fastest feedback loop for workloads affected by node failures.
 
+#### Balanced Placement
+{{< feature-state state="alpha" for_version="v0.15" >}}
+{{% alert title="Note" color="primary" %}}
+`TASBalancedPlacement` is currently an alpha feature and is disabled by default.
+
+You can enable it by editing the `TASBalancedPlacement` feature gate. Refer to the
+[Installation guide](/docs/installation/#change-the-feature-gates-configuration)
+for instructions on configuring feature gates.
+{{% /alert %}}
+
+The balanced placement algorithm provides an alternative to the greedy packing strategies. Instead of
+iterating over the domains sorted from largest to smallest available space (or based on some other criteria)
+and trying to pack as many pods/slices as possible to each domain until the request fits, it first finds the
+optimal set of domains that fit the request and then distributes the pods/slices as evenly as possible across
+these domains.
+
+Greedy placement strategies (such as `BestFit` and `LeastFreeCapacity`) might result in a placement with a small
+number of pods assigned to the last considered domain. For example 12 pods distributed among domains with
+capacities (10,10) will be placed (10,2). However, in some applications, a more balanced placement (6,6) would
+be more efficient. Some examples of such cases would be all-to-all communication procedures (e.g. Allgather)
+since more balanced placement leads to more efficient cross-domain traffic.
+
+To use this feature, use the `kueue.x-k8s.io/podset-preferred-topology` annotation on the Job. Kueue TAS make 
+sure that the minimum number of pods (or slices) placed on any domain **one level below** the indicated level
+will be maximied. Also (as a second criteria) the number of domains used on the indicated level will be
```
